I also oil-pull (and until this, flossed) in addition to brushing but found the Waterpik to be more effective than flossing. I oil-pull first, then brush my teeth, and then use the Waterpik flosser. Oil pulling is very effective for dislodging food debris but even after oil-pulling and brushing, I have found the Waterpik still gets out remaining difficult to budge food bits. I have been amazed at the tiny, tiny bits of food that end up in the sink after water-flossing. This has been a great water flosser and I appreciate it far more than flossing itself. It calls for using cold water (regular temp) but I found that using regular temp water turned out to be too chilly for my teeth and gums. Instead, I use tepid (lukewarm) water which works out wonderful! They also give 3 pressure settings which is nice. At first, it took a bit of getting used to operating the handle because I have severe rheumatoid arthritis in my hands but once I messed around with it and became familiar with holding it in different ways, it has turned out to be a great little device. Would enjoy seeing this offered in other colors, although the green is fine. Great investment, good quality and not too expensive. What more could one ask for?
